<p><b>Astrology</b> is the study of the movements and relative positions of celestial objects as a means for <a href="/wiki/Divination" title="Divination">divining</a> information about human affairs and terrestrial events.<sup id="cite_ref-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-1">[1]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2">[2]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-3">[3]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-4">[4]</a></sup> Astrology has been dated to at least the 2nd millennium <a href="/wiki/BCE" class="mw-redirect" title="BCE">BCE</a>, and has its roots in <a href="/wiki/Calendrical_calculation" title="Calendrical calculation">calendrical</a> systems used to predict seasonal shifts and to interpret celestial cycles as signs of divine communications.<sup id="cite_ref-Koch-Westenholz_1995_Foreword.2C_11_5-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Koch-Westenholz_1995_Foreword.2C_11-5">[5]</a></sup> Many cultures have attached importance to astronomical events, and some â€“ such as the <a href="/wiki/Hindu_astrology" title="Hindu astrology">Indians</a>, <a href="/wiki/Chinese_astrology" title="Chinese astrology">Chinese</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Maya_civilization" title="Maya civilization">Maya</a> â€“ developed elaborate systems for predicting terrestrial events from celestial observations. <a href="/wiki/Western_world" title="Western world">Western</a> astrology, one of the oldest astrological systems still in use, can trace its roots to 19th-17th century <a href="/wiki/Common_Era" title="Common Era">BCE</a> <a href="/wiki/Mesopotamia" title="Mesopotamia">Mesopotamia</a>, from which it spread to <a href="/wiki/Ancient_Greece" title="Ancient Greece">Ancient Greece</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ancient_Rome" title="Ancient Rome">Rome</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Arab_world" title="Arab world">Arab world</a> and eventually <a href="/wiki/Central_Europe" title="Central Europe">Central</a> and <a href="/wiki/Western_Europe" title="Western Europe">Western Europe</a>. Contemporary Western astrology is often associated with systems of <a href="/wiki/Horoscope" title="Horoscope">horoscopes</a> that purport to explain aspects of a person's <a href="/wiki/Personality" title="Personality">personality</a> and predict significant events in their lives based on the positions of celestial objects; the majority of professional astrologers rely on such systems.<sup id="cite_ref-Cosmic_6-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Cosmic-6">[6]</a></sup><sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">:83</sup></p>
<p>Throughout most of its history astrology was considered a scholarly tradition and was common in academic circles, often in close relation with <a href="/wiki/Astronomy" title="Astronomy">astronomy</a>, <a href="/wiki/Alchemy" title="Alchemy">alchemy</a>, <a href="/wiki/Meteorology" title="Meteorology">meteorology</a>, and medicine.<sup id="cite_ref-Kassell_7-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Kassell-7">[7]</a></sup> It was present in political circles, and is mentioned in various works of literature, from <a href="/wiki/Dante_Alighieri" title="Dante Alighieri">Dante Alighieri</a> and <a href="/wiki/Geoffrey_Chaucer" title="Geoffrey Chaucer">Geoffrey Chaucer</a> to <a href="/wiki/William_Shakespeare" title="William Shakespeare">William Shakespeare</a>, <a href="/wiki/Lope_de_Vega" title="Lope de Vega">Lope de Vega</a> and <a href="/wiki/Calder%C3%B3n_de_la_Barca" class="mw-redirect" title="CalderÃ³n de la Barca">CalderÃ³n de la Barca</a>.</p>
<p>With the onset of the <a href="/wiki/Scientific_revolution" title="Scientific revolution">scientific revolution</a> astrology was called into question; it has been challenged successfully both on <a href="/wiki/Scientific_theory" title="Scientific theory">theoretical</a><sup id="cite_ref-Vishveshwara_8-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Vishveshwara-8">[8]</a></sup><sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">:249;</sup><sup id="cite_ref-AsquithNSF_9-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-AsquithNSF-9">[9]</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Experiment" title="Experiment">experimental</a><sup id="cite_ref-Carlson_10-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Carlson-10">[10]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Zarka_11-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Zarka-11">[11]</a></sup> grounds, and has been shown to have no <a href="/wiki/Science" title="Science">scientific</a> validity<sup id="cite_ref-Cosmic_6-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Cosmic-6">[6]</a></sup> or <a href="/wiki/Explanatory_power" title="Explanatory power">explanatory power</a>. Astrology thus lost its academic and theoretical standing, and common belief in it has largely declined.<sup id="cite_ref-Brit_12-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Brit-12">[12]</a></sup> Astrology is now recognized to be <a href="/wiki/Pseudoscience" title="Pseudoscience">pseudoscience</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Thagard_13-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Thagard-13">[13]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-14" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-14">[14]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-SandPSandAstroSoc_15-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-SandPSandAstroSoc-15">[15]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-astrosociety.org_16-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-astrosociety.org-16">[16]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Hartmann_17-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Hartmann-17">[17]</a></sup></p>
<p></p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Etymology">Etymology</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Astrology&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Etymology">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Marcantonio_Raimondi_-_Two_Women_with_the_Signs_of_Libra_and_Scorpio.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f6/Marcantonio_Raimondi_-_Two_Women_with_the_Signs_of_Libra_and_Scorpio.jpg/170px-Marcantonio_Raimondi_-_Two_Women_with_the_Signs_of_Libra_and_Scorpio.jpg" width="170" height="245" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f6/Marcantonio_Raimondi_-_Two_Women_with_the_Signs_of_Libra_and_Scorpio.jpg/255px-Marcantonio_Raimondi_-_Two_Women_with_the_Signs_of_Libra_and_Scorpio.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f6/Marcantonio_Raimondi_-_Two_Women_with_the_Signs_of_Libra_and_Scorpio.jpg/340px-Marcantonio_Raimondi_-_Two_Women_with_the_Signs_of_Libra_and_Scorpio.jpg 2x" data-file-width="403" data-file-height="580" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Marcantonio_Raimondi_-_Two_Women_with_the_Signs_of_Libra_and_Scorpio.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Marcantonio Raimondi engraving, 15th century</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The word <i><a href="//en.wiktionary.org/wiki/astrology" class="extiw" title="wikt:astrology">astrology</a></i> comes from the early <a href="/wiki/Latin" title="Latin">Latin</a> word <i><a href="//en.wiktionary.org/wiki/astrologia" class="extiw" title="wikt:astrologia">astrologia</a></i>,<sup id="cite_ref-18" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-18">[18]</a></sup> which derives from the <a href="/wiki/Ancient_Greek" title="Ancient Greek">Greek</a> <span lang="grc"><a href="//en.wiktionary.org/wiki/%E1%BC%80%CF%83%CF%84%CF%81%CE%BF%CE%BB%CE%BF%CE%B3%CE%AF%CE%B1" class="extiw" title="wikt:á¼€ÏƒÏ„Ï?Î¿Î»Î¿Î³Î¯Î±">á¼€ÏƒÏ„Ï?Î¿Î»Î¿Î³Î¯Î±</a></span>â€”from <a href="//en.wiktionary.org/wiki/%E1%BC%84%CF%83%CF%84%CF%81%CE%BF%CE%BD#Ancient_Greek" class="extiw" title="wikt:á¼„ÏƒÏ„Ï?Î¿Î½">á¼„ÏƒÏ„Ï?Î¿Î½</a> <i>astron</i> ("star") and <a href="//en.wiktionary.org/wiki/-%CE%BB%CE%BF%CE%B3%CE%AF%CE%B1#Ancient_Greek" class="extiw" title="wikt:-Î»Î¿Î³Î¯Î±">-Î»Î¿Î³Î¯Î±</a> <i>-logia</i>, ("study of"â€”"account of the stars"). <i>Astrologia</i> later passed into meaning 'star-divination' with <i><a href="//en.wiktionary.org/wiki/astronomia" class="extiw" title="wikt:astronomia">astronomia</a></i> used for the scientific term.<sup id="cite_ref-19" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-19">[19]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Astrology&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: History">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote">Main article: <a href="/wiki/History_of_astrology" title="History of astrology">History of astrology</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:P._26_%27The_Zodiac_Man%27_a_diagram_of_a_human_body_and_astrological_symbols_with_instructions_explaining_the_importance_of_astrology_from_a_medical_perspective.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/46/P._26_%27The_Zodiac_Man%27_a_diagram_of_a_human_body_and_astrological_symbols_with_instructions_explaining_the_importance_of_astrology_from_a_medical_perspective.jpg/170px-thumbnail.jpg" width="170" height="240" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/46/P._26_%27The_Zodiac_Man%27_a_diagram_of_a_human_body_and_astrological_symbols_with_instructions_explaining_the_importance_of_astrology_from_a_medical_perspective.jpg/255px-thumbnail.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/46/P._26_%27The_Zodiac_Man%27_a_diagram_of_a_human_body_and_astrological_symbols_with_instructions_explaining_the_importance_of_astrology_from_a_medical_perspective.jpg/340px-thumbnail.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1325" data-file-height="1869" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:P._26_%27The_Zodiac_Man%27_a_diagram_of_a_human_body_and_astrological_symbols_with_instructions_explaining_the_importance_of_astrology_from_a_medical_perspective.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<i>The Zodiac Man</i> a diagram of a human body and astrological symbols with instructions explaining the importance of astrology from a medical perspective. From a 15th-century Welsh manuscript</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Many cultures have attached importance to astronomical events, and the <a href="/wiki/Hindu_astrology" title="Hindu astrology">Indians</a>, <a href="/wiki/Chinese_astrology" title="Chinese astrology">Chinese</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Maya_civilization" title="Maya civilization">Maya</a> developed elaborate systems for predicting terrestrial events from celestial observations. In the West, astrology most often consists of a system of <a href="/wiki/Horoscope" title="Horoscope">horoscopes</a> purporting to explain aspects of a person's <a href="/wiki/Personality" title="Personality">personality</a> and predict future events in their life based on the positions of the sun, moon, and other celestial objects at the time of their birth. The majority of professional astrologers rely on such systems.<sup id="cite_ref-Cosmic_6-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Cosmic-6">[6]</a></sup><sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">:83</sup></p>
<p>Astrology has been dated to at least the 2nd millennium <a href="/wiki/BCE" class="mw-redirect" title="BCE">BCE</a>, with roots in <a href="/wiki/Calendrical_calculation" title="Calendrical calculation">calendrical</a> systems used to predict seasonal shifts and to interpret celestial cycles as signs of divine communications.<sup id="cite_ref-Koch-Westenholz_1995_Foreword.2C_11_5-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Koch-Westenholz_1995_Foreword.2C_11-5">[5]</a></sup> A form of astrology was practised in the first dynasty of <a href="/wiki/Mesopotamia" title="Mesopotamia">Mesopotamia</a> (1950â€“1651 BCE). Chinese astrology was elaborated in the <a href="/wiki/Zhou_dynasty" title="Zhou dynasty">Zhou dynasty</a> (1046â€“256 BCE). <a href="/wiki/Hellenistic_astrology" title="Hellenistic astrology">Hellenistic astrology</a> after 332 BCE mixed <a href="/wiki/Babylonian_astrology" title="Babylonian astrology">Babylonian astrology</a> with Egyptian <a href="/wiki/Decans" title="Decans">Decanic astrology</a> in <a href="/wiki/Alexandria" title="Alexandria">Alexandria</a>, creating <a href="/wiki/Horoscopic_astrology" title="Horoscopic astrology">horoscopic astrology</a>. <a href="/wiki/Alexander_the_Great" title="Alexander the Great">Alexander the Great's</a> conquest of <a href="/wiki/Asia" title="Asia">Asia</a> allowed astrology to spread to <a href="/wiki/Ancient_Greece" title="Ancient Greece">Ancient Greece</a> and <a href="/wiki/Ancient_Rome" title="Ancient Rome">Rome</a>. In Rome, astrology was associated with '<a href="/wiki/Chaldea" title="Chaldea">Chaldean</a> wisdom'. After the conquest of Alexandria in the 7th century, astrology was taken up by Islamic scholars, and Hellenistic texts were translated into Arabic and Persian. In the 12th century, Arabic texts were imported to Europe and <a href="/wiki/Latin_translations_of_the_12th_century" title="Latin translations of the 12th century">translated into Latin</a>. Major astronomers including <a href="/wiki/Tycho_Brahe" title="Tycho Brahe">Tycho Brahe</a>, <a href="/wiki/Johannes_Kepler" title="Johannes Kepler">Johannes Kepler</a> and <a href="/wiki/Galileo" class="mw-redirect" title="Galileo">Galileo</a> practised as court astrologers. Astrological references appear in literature in the works of poets such as <a href="/wiki/Dante_Alighieri" title="Dante Alighieri">Dante Alighieri</a> and <a href="/wiki/Geoffrey_Chaucer" title="Geoffrey Chaucer">Geoffrey Chaucer</a>, and of playwrights such as <a href="/wiki/Christopher_Marlowe" title="Christopher Marlowe">Christopher Marlowe</a> and <a href="/wiki/William_Shakespeare" title="William Shakespeare">William Shakespeare</a>.</p>
<p>Throughout most of its history, astrology was considered a scholarly tradition. It was accepted in political and academic contexts, and was connected with other studies, such as <a href="/wiki/Astronomy" title="Astronomy">astronomy</a>, <a href="/wiki/Alchemy" title="Alchemy">alchemy</a>, <a href="/wiki/Meteorology" title="Meteorology">meteorology</a>, and medicine.<sup id="cite_ref-Kassell_7-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Kassell-7">[7]</a></sup> At the end of the 17th century, new scientific concepts in astronomy and physics (such as <a href="/wiki/Heliocentrism" title="Heliocentrism">heliocentrism</a> and <a href="/wiki/Classical_mechanics" title="Classical mechanics">Newtonian mechanics</a>) called astrology into question. Astrology thus lost its academic and theoretical standing, and common belief in astrology has largely declined.<sup id="cite_ref-Brit_12-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Brit-12">[12]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Ancient_world">Ancient world</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Astrology&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Ancient world">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote">See also: <a href="/wiki/Babylonian_astrology" title="Babylonian astrology">Babylonian astrology</a></div>
<p>Astrology, in its broadest sense, is the search for meaning in the sky.<sup id="cite_ref-20" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-20">[20]</a></sup><sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">:2,3</sup> Early evidence for humans making conscious attempts to measure, record, and predict seasonal changes by reference to astronomical cycles, appears as markings on bones and cave walls, which show that lunar cycles were being noted as early as 25,000 years ago.<sup id="cite_ref-Marshack_21-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Marshack-21">[21]</a></sup><sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">:81ff</sup> This was a first step towards recording the Moon's influence upon tides and rivers, and towards organising a communal calendar.<sup id="cite_ref-Marshack_21-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Marshack-21">[21]</a></sup> Farmers addressed agricultural needs with increasing knowledge of the <a href="/wiki/Constellations" class="mw-redirect" title="Constellations">constellations</a> that appear in the different seasonsâ€”and used the rising of particular star-groups to herald annual floods or seasonal activities.<sup id="cite_ref-22" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-22">[22]</a></sup> By the 3rd millennium BCE, civilisations had sophisticated awareness of celestial cycles, and may have oriented temples in alignment with <a href="/wiki/Heliacal_rising" title="Heliacal rising">heliacal risings</a> of the stars.<sup id="cite_ref-23" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-23">[23]</a></sup></p>
<p>Scattered evidence suggests that the oldest known astrological references are copies of texts made in the ancient world. The <a href="/wiki/Venus_tablet_of_Ammisaduqa" title="Venus tablet of Ammisaduqa">Venus tablet of Ammisaduqa</a> thought to be compiled in <a href="/wiki/Babylon" title="Babylon">Babylon</a> around 1700 BCE.<sup id="cite_ref-24" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-24">[24]</a></sup> A scroll documenting an early use of <a href="/wiki/Electional_astrology" title="Electional astrology">electional astrology</a> is doubtfully ascribed to the reign of the <a href="/wiki/Sumer" title="Sumer">Sumerian</a> ruler <a href="/wiki/Gudea_of_Lagash" class="mw-redirect" title="Gudea of Lagash">Gudea of Lagash</a> (c. 2144 â€“ 2124 BCE). This describes how the gods revealed to him in a dream the constellations that would be most favourable for the planned construction of a temple.<sup id="cite_ref-25" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-25">[25]</a></sup> However, there is controversy about whether these were genuinely recorded at the time or merely ascribed to ancient rulers by posterity. The oldest undisputed evidence of the use of astrology as an integrated system of knowledge is therefore attributed to the records of the first dynasty of <a href="/wiki/Mesopotamia" title="Mesopotamia">Mesopotamia</a> (1950â€“1651 BCE). This astrology had some parallels with <a href="/wiki/Hellenistic" class="mw-redirect" title="Hellenistic">Hellenistic</a> Greek (western) astrology, including the zodiac, a norming point near 9 degrees in Aries, the trine aspect, planetary exaltations, and the dodekatemoria (the twelve divisions of 30 degrees each).<sup id="cite_ref-Rochberg-Halton_26-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Rochberg-Halton-26">[26]</a></sup> The Babylonians viewed celestial events as possible signs rather than as causes of physical events.<sup id="cite_ref-Rochberg-Halton_26-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Rochberg-Halton-26">[26]</a></sup></p>
<p>The system of <a href="/wiki/Chinese_astrology" title="Chinese astrology">Chinese astrology</a> was elaborated during the <a href="/wiki/Zhou_dynasty" title="Zhou dynasty">Zhou dynasty</a> (1046â€“256 BCE) and flourished during the <a href="/wiki/Han_Dynasty" class="mw-redirect" title="Han Dynasty">Han Dynasty</a> (2nd century BCE to 2nd century CE), during which all the familiar elements of traditional Chinese culture â€“ the Yin-Yang philosophy, theory of the five elements, Heaven and Earth, Confucian morality â€“ were brought together to formalise the philosophical principles of Chinese medicine and divination, astrology and alchemy.<sup id="cite_ref-Kistemaker_27-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Kistemaker-27">[27]</a></sup><sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">:3,4</sup></p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Ancient_objections">Ancient objections</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Astrology&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Ancient objections">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Cicero_-_Musei_Capitolini.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/40/Cicero_-_Musei_Capitolini.JPG/170px-Cicero_-_Musei_Capitolini.JPG" width="170" height="227" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/40/Cicero_-_Musei_Capitolini.JPG/255px-Cicero_-_Musei_Capitolini.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/40/Cicero_-_Musei_Capitolini.JPG/340px-Cicero_-_Musei_Capitolini.JPG 2x" data-file-width="1227" data-file-height="1636" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Cicero_-_Musei_Capitolini.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The Roman orator <a href="/wiki/Cicero" title="Cicero">Cicero</a> objected to astrology</div>
</div>
</div>
<p><a href="/wiki/Cicero" title="Cicero">Cicero</a> stated the twins objection (that with close birth times, personal outcomes can be very different), later developed by <a href="/wiki/Saint_Augustine" class="mw-redirect" title="Saint Augustine">Saint Augustine</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-28" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-28">[28]</a></sup> He argued that since the other planets are much more distant from the earth than the moon, they could have only very tiny influence compared to the moon's.<sup id="cite_ref-29" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-29">[29]</a></sup> He also argued that if astrology explains everything about a person's fate, then it wrongly ignores the visible effect of inherited ability and parenting, changes in health worked by medicine, or the effects of the weather on people.<sup id="cite_ref-30" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-30">[30]</a></sup></p>
<p><a href="/wiki/Plotinus" title="Plotinus">Plotinus</a> argued that since the fixed stars are much more distant than the planets, it is laughable to imagine the planets' effect on mankind should depend on their position with respect to the zodiac. He also argues that the interpretation of the moon's conjunction with a planet as good when the moon is full, but bad when the moon is waning, is clearly wrong, as from the moon's point of view, half of her surface is always in sunlight; and from the planet's point of view, waning should be better, as then the planet sees some light from the moon, but when the moon is full to us, it is dark, and therefore bad, on the side facing the planet.<sup id="cite_ref-31" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-31">[31]</a></sup></p>
<p><a href="/wiki/Favorinus" title="Favorinus">Favorinus</a> argued that it was absurd to imagine that stars and planets would affect human bodies in the same way as they affect the tides,<sup id="cite_ref-32" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-32">[32]</a></sup> and equally absurd that small motions in the heavens cause large changes in people's fates. <a href="/wiki/Sextus_Empiricus" title="Sextus Empiricus">Sextus Empiricus</a> argued that it was absurd to link human attributes with myths about the signs of the zodiac.<sup id="cite_ref-33" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-33">[33]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Carneades" title="Carneades">Carneades</a> argued that belief in fate denies <a href="/wiki/Free_will" title="Free will">free will</a> and <a href="/wiki/Morality" title="Morality">morality</a>; that people born at different times can all die in the same accident or battle; and that contrary to uniform influences from the stars, tribes and cultures are all different.<sup id="cite_ref-34" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-34">[34]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Hellenistic_Egypt">Hellenistic Egypt</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Astrology&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Hellenistic Egypt">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Hellenistic_astrology" title="Hellenistic astrology">Hellenistic astrology</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Quadritpartitum.jpg" class="image"><img alt="Ptolemy's Tetrabiblos, the Hellenistic text that founded Western astrology" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ad/Quadritpartitum.jpg/170px-Quadritpartitum.jpg" width="170" height="205" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ad/Quadritpartitum.jpg/255px-Quadritpartitum.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ad/Quadritpartitum.jpg/340px-Quadritpartitum.jpg 2x" data-file-width="419" data-file-height="505" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Quadritpartitum.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
1484 copy of first page of <a href="/wiki/Ptolemy" title="Ptolemy">Ptolemy's</a> <i>Tetrabiblos</i>, translated into Latin by <a href="/wiki/Plato_of_Tivoli" class="mw-redirect" title="Plato of Tivoli">Plato of Tivoli</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>In 525 BCE, Egypt was conquered by the Persians. The 1st century BCE Egyptian <a href="/wiki/Dendera_Zodiac" class="mw-redirect" title="Dendera Zodiac">Dendera Zodiac</a> shares two signs â€“ the Balance and the Scorpion â€“ with Mesopotamian astrology.<sup id="cite_ref-35" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-35">[35]</a></sup></p>
<p>With the occupation by <a href="/wiki/Alexander_the_Great" title="Alexander the Great">Alexander the Great</a> in 332 BCE, Egypt became <a href="/wiki/Hellenistic" class="mw-redirect" title="Hellenistic">Hellenistic</a>. The city of <a href="/wiki/Alexandria" title="Alexandria">Alexandria</a> was founded by Alexander after the conquest, becoming the place where <a href="/wiki/Babylonian_astrology" title="Babylonian astrology">Babylonian astrology</a> was mixed with Egyptian <a href="/wiki/Decans" title="Decans">Decanic astrology</a> to create <a href="/wiki/Horoscopic_astrology" title="Horoscopic astrology">Horoscopic astrology</a>. This contained the Babylonian zodiac with its system of planetary <a href="/wiki/Exaltation_(astrology)" title="Exaltation (astrology)">exaltations</a>, the triplicities of the signs and the importance of eclipses. It used the Egyptian concept of dividing the zodiac into thirty-six decans of ten degrees each, with an emphasis on the rising decan, and the Greek system of planetary Gods, sign rulership and <a href="/wiki/Four_elements" class="mw-redirect" title="Four elements">four elements</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-36" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-36">[36]</a></sup> 2nd century BCE texts predict positions of planets in zodiac signs at the time of the rising of certain decans, particularly Sothis.<sup id="cite_ref-37" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-37">[37]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Astrologer" class="mw-redirect" title="Astrologer">astrologer</a> and astronomer <a href="/wiki/Ptolemy#Astrology" title="Ptolemy">Ptolemy</a> lived in Alexandria. Ptolemy's work the <i><a href="/wiki/Tetrabiblos" title="Tetrabiblos">Tetrabiblos</a></i> formed the basis of Western astrology, and, "...enjoyed almost the authority of a Bible among the astrological writers of a thousand years or more."<sup id="cite_ref-38" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-38">[38]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Greece_and_Rome">Greece and Rome</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Astrology&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Greece and Rome">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The conquest of <a href="/wiki/Asia" title="Asia">Asia</a> by <a href="/wiki/Alexander_the_Great" title="Alexander the Great">Alexander the Great</a> exposed the Greeks to ideas from <a href="/wiki/Syria" title="Syria">Syria</a>, Babylon, Persia and central Asia.<sup id="cite_ref-39" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-39">[39]</a></sup> Around 280 BCE, <a href="/wiki/Berossus" title="Berossus">Berossus</a>, a priest of <a href="/wiki/Marduk" title="Marduk">Bel</a> from Babylon, moved to the Greek island of <a href="/wiki/Kos" title="Kos">Kos</a>, teaching astrology and Babylonian culture.<sup id="cite_ref-40" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-40">[40]</a></sup> By the 1st century BCE, there were two varieties of astrology, one using <a href="/wiki/Horoscope" title="Horoscope">horoscopes</a> to describe the past, present and future; the other, <a href="/wiki/Theurgic" class="mw-redirect" title="Theurgic">theurgic</a>, emphasising the <a href="/wiki/Soul" title="Soul">soul's</a> ascent to the stars.<sup id="cite_ref-41" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-41">[41]</a></sup> Greek influence played a crucial role in the transmission of astrological theory to <a href="/wiki/Ancient_Rome" title="Ancient Rome">Rome</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-B32_42-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-B32-42">[42]</a></sup></p>
<p>The first definite reference to astrology in Rome comes from the orator <a href="/wiki/Cato_the_Elder" title="Cato the Elder">Cato</a>, who in 160 BCE warned farm overseers against consulting with Chaldeans,<sup id="cite_ref-43" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-43">[43]</a></sup> who were described as Babylonian 'star-gazers'.<sup id="cite_ref-Campion227_44-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Campion227-44">[44]</a></sup> Among both Greeks and <a href="/wiki/Ancient_Rome" title="Ancient Rome">Romans</a>, Babylonia (also known as <a href="/wiki/Chaldea" title="Chaldea">Chaldea</a>) became so identified with astrology that 'Chaldean wisdom' became <a href="/wiki/Synonym" title="Synonym">synonymous</a> with <a href="/wiki/Divination" title="Divination">divination</a> using planets and stars.<sup id="cite_ref-45" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-45">[45]</a></sup> The 2nd-century Roman poet and satirist <a href="/wiki/Juvenal" title="Juvenal">Juvenal</a> complains about the pervasive influence of Chaldeans, saying, "Still more trusted are the Chaldaeans; every word uttered by the astrologer they will believe has come from <a href="/wiki/Jupiter_(mythology)" title="Jupiter (mythology)">Hammon's</a> fountain."<sup id="cite_ref-46" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-46">[46]</a></sup></p>
<p>One of the first astrologers to bring <a href="/wiki/Hermeticism" title="Hermeticism">Hermetic</a> astrology to Rome was <a href="/wiki/Thrasyllus_of_Mendes" title="Thrasyllus of Mendes">Thrasyllus</a>, astrologer to the <a href="/wiki/Emperor" title="Emperor">emperor</a> <a href="/wiki/Tiberius" title="Tiberius">Tiberius</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-B32_42-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-B32-42">[42]</a></sup> the first emperor to have had a court astrologer,<sup id="cite_ref-47" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-47">[47]</a></sup> though his predecessor <a href="/wiki/Augustus" title="Augustus">Augustus</a> had used astrology to help legitimise his <a href="/wiki/Imperialism" title="Imperialism">Imperial</a> rights.<sup id="cite_ref-48" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-48">[48]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Medieval_world">Medieval world</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Astrology&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Medieval world">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Hindu">Hindu</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Astrology&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Hindu">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>The main texts upon which classical Indian astrology is based are early medieval compilations, notably the <i><a href="/wiki/B%E1%B9%9Bhat_Par%C4%81%C5%9Bara_Hor%C4%81%C5%9B%C4%81stra" class="mw-redirect" title="Bá¹›hat ParÄ?Å›ara HorÄ?Å›Ä?stra"><span title="International Alphabet of Sanskrit Transliteration" class="Unicode" style="white-space:normal; text-decoration: none">Bá¹›hat ParÄ?Å›ara HorÄ?Å›Ä?stra</span></a></i>, and <i><a href="/wiki/S%C4%81r%C4%81val%C4%AB" title="SÄ?rÄ?valÄ«">SÄ?rÄ?valÄ«</a></i> by <span title="International Alphabet of Sanskrit Transliteration" class="Unicode" style="white-space:normal; text-decoration: none">KalyÄ?á¹‡avarma</span>. The <i>HorÄ?shastra</i> is a composite work of 71 chapters, of which the first part (chapters 1â€“51) dates to the 7th to early 8th centuries and the second part (chapters 52â€“71) to the later 8th century. The <i>SÄ?rÄ?valÄ«</i> likewise dates to around 800 CE.<sup id="cite_ref-49" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-49">[49]</a></sup> English translations of these texts were published by N.N. Krishna Rau and V.B. Choudhari in 1963 and 1961, respectively.</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Islamic">Islamic</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Astrology&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Islamic">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<div role="note" class="hatnote">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Astrology_in_medieval_Islam" title="Astrology in medieval Islam">Astrology in medieval Islam</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Translation_of_Albumasar_Venice_1515_De_Magnis_Coniunctionibus.jpg" class="image"><img alt="Image of a Latin astrological text" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5c/Translation_of_Albumasar_Venice_1515_De_Magnis_Coniunctionibus.jpg/220px-Translation_of_Albumasar_Venice_1515_De_Magnis_Coniunctionibus.jpg" width="220" height="148" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5c/Translation_of_Albumasar_Venice_1515_De_Magnis_Coniunctionibus.jpg/330px-Translation_of_Albumasar_Venice_1515_De_Magnis_Coniunctionibus.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5c/Translation_of_Albumasar_Venice_1515_De_Magnis_Coniunctionibus.jpg/440px-Translation_of_Albumasar_Venice_1515_De_Magnis_Coniunctionibus.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2419" data-file-height="1622" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Translation_of_Albumasar_Venice_1515_De_Magnis_Coniunctionibus.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Latin" title="Latin">Latin</a> translation of <a href="/wiki/Albumasar" class="mw-redirect" title="Albumasar">AbÅ« MaÊ¿shar's</a> <i>De Magnis Coniunctionibus</i> ('Of the great <a href="/wiki/Conjunction_(astronomy_and_astrology)" class="mw-redirect" title="Conjunction (astronomy and astrology)">conjunctions</a>'), <a href="/wiki/Venice" title="Venice">Venice</a>, 1515</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Astrology was taken up by Islamic scholars<sup id="cite_ref-50" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-50">[50]</a></sup> following the collapse of <a href="/wiki/Alexandria" title="Alexandria">Alexandria</a> to the Arabs in the 7th century, and the founding of the <a href="/wiki/Abbasid_Caliphate" title="Abbasid Caliphate">Abbasid empire</a> in the 8th. The second Abbasid <a href="/wiki/Caliph" class="mw-redirect" title="Caliph">caliph</a>, <a href="/wiki/Al_Mansur" class="mw-redirect" title="Al Mansur">Al Mansur</a> (754â€“775) founded the city of <a href="/wiki/Baghdad" title="Baghdad">Baghdad</a> to act as a centre of learning, and included in its design a library-translation centre known as <i>Bayt al-Hikma</i> 'House of Wisdom', which continued to receive development from his heirs and was to provide a major impetus for Arabic-Persian translations of Hellenistic astrological texts. The early translators included <a href="/wiki/Mashallah_ibn_Athari" title="Mashallah ibn Athari">Mashallah</a>, who helped to elect the time for the foundation of Baghdad,<sup id="cite_ref-Biruni_51-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Biruni-51">[51]</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Sahl_ibn_Bishr" title="Sahl ibn Bishr">Sahl ibn Bishr</a>, (<i>a.k.a.</i> <i>Zael</i>), whose texts were directly influential upon later European astrologers such as <a href="/wiki/Guido_Bonatti" title="Guido Bonatti">Guido Bonatti</a> in the 13th century, and <a href="/wiki/William_Lilly" title="William Lilly">William Lilly</a> in the 17th century.<sup id="cite_ref-52" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-52">[52]</a></sup> Knowledge of Arabic texts started to become imported into Europe during the <a href="/wiki/Latin_translations_of_the_12th_century" title="Latin translations of the 12th century">Latin translations of the 12th century</a>.</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Europe">Europe</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Astrology&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Europe">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Meister_von_San_Vitale_in_Ravenna.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/89/Meister_von_San_Vitale_in_Ravenna.jpg/170px-Meister_von_San_Vitale_in_Ravenna.jpg" width="170" height="230" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/89/Meister_von_San_Vitale_in_Ravenna.jpg/255px-Meister_von_San_Vitale_in_Ravenna.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/89/Meister_von_San_Vitale_in_Ravenna.jpg/340px-Meister_von_San_Vitale_in_Ravenna.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1409" data-file-height="1907" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Meister_von_San_Vitale_in_Ravenna.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Dante_Alighieri" title="Dante Alighieri">Dante Alighieri</a> meets the Emperor <a href="/wiki/Justinian_I" title="Justinian I">Justinian</a> in the Sphere of <a href="/wiki/Mercury_(planet)" title="Mercury (planet)">Mercury</a>, in Canto 5 of the <i><a href="/wiki/Paradiso_(Dante)" title="Paradiso (Dante)">Paradiso</a></i></div>
</div>
</div>
<div role="note" class="hatnote">See also: <a href="/wiki/Christian_views_on_astrology" title="Christian views on astrology">Christian views on astrology</a></div>
<p>The first astrological book published in Europe was the <i>Liber Planetis et Mundi Climatibus</i> ("Book of the Planets and Regions of the World"), which appeared between 1010 and 1027 AD, and may have been authored by <a href="/wiki/Gerbert_of_Aurillac" class="mw-redirect" title="Gerbert of Aurillac">Gerbert of Aurillac</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Campion44_53-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Campion44-53">[53]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Ptolemy" title="Ptolemy">Ptolemy's</a> second century AD <i><a href="/wiki/Tetrabiblos" title="Tetrabiblos">Tetrabiblos</a></i> was translated into Latin by <a href="/wiki/Plato_Tiburtinus" title="Plato Tiburtinus">Plato of Tivoli</a> in 1138.<sup id="cite_ref-Campion44_53-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Campion44-53">[53]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Dominican_order" class="mw-redirect" title="Dominican order">Dominican</a> theologian <a href="/wiki/Thomas_Aquinas" title="Thomas Aquinas">Thomas Aquinas</a> followed <a href="/wiki/Aristotle" title="Aristotle">Aristotle</a> in proposing that the stars ruled the imperfect 'sublunary' body, while attempting to reconcile astrology with Christianity by stating that God ruled the soul.<sup id="cite_ref-Campion45_54-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Campion45-54">[54]</a></sup> The thirteenth century mathematician <a href="/wiki/Campanus_of_Novara" title="Campanus of Novara">Campanus of Novara</a> is said to have devised a system of astrological houses that divides the <a href="/wiki/Prime_vertical" title="Prime vertical">prime vertical</a> into 'houses' of equal 30Â° arcs,<sup id="cite_ref-Campion46_55-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Campion46-55">[55]</a></sup> though the system was used earlier in the East.<sup id="cite_ref-56" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-56">[56]</a></sup> The thirteenth century <a href="/wiki/Astronomer" title="Astronomer">astronomer</a> <a href="/wiki/Guido_Bonatti" title="Guido Bonatti">Guido Bonatti</a> wrote a textbook, the <i>Liber Astronomicus</i>, a copy of which King <a href="/wiki/Henry_VII_of_England" title="Henry VII of England">Henry VII of England</a> owned at the end of the fifteenth century.<sup id="cite_ref-Campion46_55-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Campion46-55">[55]</a></sup></p>
<p>In <i><a href="/wiki/Paradiso_(Dante)" title="Paradiso (Dante)">Paradiso</a></i>, the final part of the <i><a href="/wiki/Divine_Comedy" title="Divine Comedy">Divine Comedy</a></i>, the Italian poet <a href="/wiki/Dante_Alighieri" title="Dante Alighieri">Dante Alighieri</a> referred "in countless details"<sup id="cite_ref-Durling_57-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Durling-57">[57]</a></sup> to the astrological planets, though he adapted traditional astrology to suit his Christian viewpoint,<sup id="cite_ref-Durling_57-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Durling-57">[57]</a></sup> for example using astrological thinking in his prophecies of the reform of Christendom.<sup id="cite_ref-58" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-58">[58]</a></sup></p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Medieval_objections">Medieval objections</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Astrology&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Medieval objections">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Isidor_von_Sevilla.jpeg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/79/Isidor_von_Sevilla.jpeg/170px-Isidor_von_Sevilla.jpeg" width="170" height="189" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/79/Isidor_von_Sevilla.jpeg/255px-Isidor_von_Sevilla.jpeg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/79/Isidor_von_Sevilla.jpeg/340px-Isidor_von_Sevilla.jpeg 2x" data-file-width="2705" data-file-height="3009" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Isidor_von_Sevilla.jpeg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The medieval theologian <a href="/wiki/Isidore_of_Seville" title="Isidore of Seville">Isidore of Seville</a> criticised the predictive part of astrology</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>In the seventh century, <a href="/wiki/Isidore_of_Seville" title="Isidore of Seville">Isidore of Seville</a> argued in his <i><a href="/wiki/Etymologiae" title="Etymologiae">Etymologiae</a></i> that astronomy described the movements of the heavens, while astrology had two parts: one was scientific, describing the movements of the sun, the moon and the stars, while the other, making predictions, was theologically erroneous.<sup id="cite_ref-Wood5_59-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Wood5-59">[59]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Isidore_60-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Isidore-60">[60]</a></sup> In contrast, <a href="/wiki/John_Gower" title="John Gower">John Gower</a> in the fourteenth century defined astrology as essentially limited to the making of predictions.<sup id="cite_ref-Wood5_59-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Wood5-59">[59]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-61" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-61">[61]</a></sup> The influence of the stars was in turn divided into natural astrology, with for example effects on tides and the growth of plants, and judicial astrology, with supposedly predictable effects on people.<sup id="cite_ref-Wood6_62-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Wood6-62">[62]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Allen148_63-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Allen148-63">[63]</a></sup> The fourteenth century sceptic <a href="/wiki/Nicole_Oresme" title="Nicole Oresme">Nicole Oresme</a> however included astronomy as a part of astrology in his <i>Livre de divinacions</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-Wood8_64-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Wood8-64">[64]</a></sup> Oresme argued that current approaches to prediction of events such as plagues, wars, and weather were inappropriate, but that such prediction was a valid field of inquiry. However, he attacked the use of astrology to choose the timing of actions (so-called interrogation and election) as wholly false, and rejected the determination of human action by the stars on grounds of free will.<sup id="cite_ref-Wood8_64-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Wood8-64">[64]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Coopland_65-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Coopland-65">[65]</a></sup> The friar Laurens Pignon (c. 1368â€“1449)<sup id="cite_ref-66" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-66">[66]</a></sup> similarly rejected all forms of divination and determinism, including by the stars, in his 1411 <i>Contre les Devineurs</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-67" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-67">[67]</a></sup> This was in opposition to the tradition carried by the Arab astronomer <a href="/wiki/Albumasar" class="mw-redirect" title="Albumasar">Albumasar</a> (787-886) whose <i>Introductorium in Astronomiam</i> and <i>De Magnis Coniunctionibus</i> argued the view that both individual actions and larger scale history are determined by the stars.<sup id="cite_ref-68" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-68">[68]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Renaissance_and_Early_Modern">Renaissance and Early Modern</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Astrology&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Renaissance and Early Modern">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Robert_Fludd%27s_An_Astrologer_Casting_a_Horoscope_1617.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b5/Robert_Fludd%27s_An_Astrologer_Casting_a_Horoscope_1617.jpg/220px-Robert_Fludd%27s_An_Astrologer_Casting_a_Horoscope_1617.jpg" width="220" height="212" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b5/Robert_Fludd%27s_An_Astrologer_Casting_a_Horoscope_1617.jpg/330px-Robert_Fludd%27s_An_Astrologer_Casting_a_Horoscope_1617.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/b/b5/Robert_Fludd%27s_An_Astrologer_Casting_a_Horoscope_1617.jpg 2x" data-file-width="400" data-file-height="386" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Robert_Fludd%27s_An_Astrologer_Casting_a_Horoscope_1617.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
'An Astrologer Casting a Horoscope' from <a href="/wiki/Robert_Fludd" title="Robert Fludd">Robert Fludd's</a> <i>Utriusque Cosmi Historia</i>, 1617</div>
</div>
</div>
<p><a href="/wiki/Renaissance" title="Renaissance">Renaissance</a> scholars commonly practised astrology. <a href="/wiki/Gerolamo_Cardano" title="Gerolamo Cardano">Gerolamo Cardano</a> cast the horoscope of king <a href="/wiki/Edward_VI_of_England" title="Edward VI of England">Edward VI of England</a>, while <a href="/wiki/John_Dee" title="John Dee">John Dee</a> was the personal astrologer to queen <a href="/wiki/Elizabeth_I_of_England" title="Elizabeth I of England">Elizabeth I of England</a>. <a href="/wiki/Catherine_de_Medici" class="mw-redirect" title="Catherine de Medici">Catherine de Medici</a> paid <a href="/wiki/Michael_Nostradamus" class="mw-redirect" title="Michael Nostradamus">Michael Nostradamus</a> in 1566 to verify the prediction of the death of her husband, king <a href="/wiki/Henry_II_of_France" title="Henry II of France">Henry II of France</a> made by her astrologer Lucus Gauricus. Major astronomers who practised as court astrologers included <a href="/wiki/Tycho_Brahe" title="Tycho Brahe">Tycho Brahe</a> in the royal court of Denmark, <a href="/wiki/Johannes_Kepler" title="Johannes Kepler">Johannes Kepler</a> to the <a href="/wiki/Habsburgs" class="mw-redirect" title="Habsburgs">Habsburgs</a>, <a href="/wiki/Galileo_Galilei" title="Galileo Galilei">Galileo Galilei</a> to the <a href="/wiki/Medici" class="mw-redirect" title="Medici">Medici</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Giordano_Bruno" title="Giordano Bruno">Giordano Bruno</a> who was burnt at the stake for heresy in Rome in 1600.<sup id="cite_ref-Campion47_69-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Campion47-69">[69]</a></sup> The distinction between astrology and astronomy was not entirely clear. Advances in astronomy were often motivated by the desire to improve the accuracy of astrology.<sup id="cite_ref-70" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-70">[70]</a></sup></p>
<p><a href="/wiki/Ephemeris" title="Ephemeris">Ephemerides</a> with complex astrological calculations, and <a href="/wiki/Almanac" title="Almanac">almanacs</a> interpreting celestial events for use in medicine and for choosing times to plant crops, were popular in Elizabethan England.<sup id="cite_ref-Harkness105_71-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Harkness105-71">[71]</a></sup> In 1597, the English <a href="/wiki/Mathematician" title="Mathematician">mathematician</a> and <a href="/wiki/Physician" title="Physician">physician</a> <a href="/wiki/Thomas_Hood_(mathematician)" title="Thomas Hood (mathematician)">Thomas Hood</a> made a set of paper instruments that used revolving overlays to help students work out relationships between fixed stars or constellations, the midheaven, and the twelve <a href="/wiki/House_(astrology)" title="House (astrology)">astrological houses</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Harkness133_72-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Harkness133-72">[72]</a></sup> Hood's instruments also illustrated, for pedagogical purposes, the supposed relationships between the signs of the zodiac, the planets, and the parts of the human body adherents believed were governed by the planets and signs.<sup id="cite_ref-Harkness133_72-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Harkness133-72">[72]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-73" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-73">[73]</a></sup> While Hood's presentation was innovative, his astrological information was largely standard and was taken from <a href="/wiki/Gerard_Mercator" class="mw-redirect" title="Gerard Mercator">Gerard Mercator's</a> astrological disc made in 1551, or a source used by Mercator.<sup id="cite_ref-74" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-74">[74]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-75" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-75">[75]</a></sup></p>
<p>English astrology had reached its zenith by the 17th century.<sup id="cite_ref-76" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-76">[76]</a></sup> Astrologers were theorists, researchers, and social engineers, as well as providing individual advice to everyone from monarchs downwards. Among other things, astrologers could advise on the best time to take a journey or harvest a crop, diagnose and prescribe for physical or mental illnesses, and predict natural disasters. This underpinned a system in which everythingâ€”people, the world, the universeâ€”was understood to be interconnected, and astrology co-existed happily with <a href="/wiki/Religion" title="Religion">religion</a>, <a href="/wiki/Magic_(paranormal)" title="Magic (paranormal)">magic</a> and <a href="/wiki/Science" title="Science">science</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-77" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-77">[77]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Enlightenment_period_and_onwards">Enlightenment period and onwards</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Astrology&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Enlightenment period and onwards">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>During <a href="/wiki/The_Enlightenment" class="mw-redirect" title="The Enlightenment">the Enlightenment</a>, intellectual sympathy for astrology fell away, leaving only a popular following supported by cheap almanacs.<sup id="cite_ref-Porter_78-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Porter-78">[78]</a></sup> One English almanac compiler, Richard Saunders, followed the spirit of the age by printing a derisive <i>Discourse on the Invalidity of Astrology</i>, while in France <a href="/wiki/Pierre_Bayle" title="Pierre Bayle">Pierre Bayle's</a> <i>Dictionnaire</i> of 1697 stated that the subject was puerile.<sup id="cite_ref-Porter_78-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Porter-78">[78]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Anglo-Irish" class="mw-redirect" title="Anglo-Irish">Anglo-Irish</a> <a href="/wiki/Satire" title="Satire">satirist</a> <a href="/wiki/Jonathan_Swift" title="Jonathan Swift">Jonathan Swift</a> ridiculed the <a href="/wiki/Whiggism" title="Whiggism">Whig</a> political astrologer <a href="/wiki/John_Partridge_(astrologer)" title="John Partridge (astrologer)">John Partridge</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Porter_78-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Porter-78">[78]</a></sup></p>
<p>Astrology saw a popular revival starting in the 19th century, as part of a general revival of <a href="/wiki/Spiritualism" title="Spiritualism">spiritualism</a> andâ€”later, <a href="/wiki/New_Age" title="New Age">New Age</a> philosophy,<sup id="cite_ref-Campion-2009_79-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Campion-2009-79">[79]</a></sup><sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">:239â€“249</sup> and through the influence of mass media such as newspaper horoscopes.<sup id="cite_ref-Campion-2009_79-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Campion-2009-79">[79]</a></sup><sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">:259â€“263</sup> Early in the 20th century the psychiatrist <a href="/wiki/Carl_Jung" title="Carl Jung">Carl Jung</a> developed some concepts concerning astrology,<sup id="cite_ref-80" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-80">[80]</a></sup> which led to the development of <a href="/wiki/Psychological_astrology" title="Psychological astrology">psychological astrology</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Campion-2009_79-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Campion-2009-79">[79]</a></sup><sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">:251â€“256;</sup><sup id="cite_ref-81" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-81">[81]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-82" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-82">[82]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Principles_and_practice">Principles and practice</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Astrology&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Principles and practice">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Advocates have defined astrology as a symbolic language, an <a href="/wiki/Art" title="Art">art</a> form, a <a href="/wiki/Science" title="Science">science</a>, and a method of divination.<sup id="cite_ref-83" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-83">[83]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-84" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-84">[84]</a></sup> Though most cultural astrology systems share common roots in ancient philosophies that influenced each other, many use methods that differ from those in the West. These include Hindu astrology (also known as "Indian astrology" and in modern times referred to as "Vedic astrology") and Chinese astrology, both of which have influenced the world's cultural history.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Western">Western</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Astrology&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Western">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote">For more details on this topic, see <a href="/wiki/Western_astrology" title="Western astrology">Western astrology</a>.</div>
<p><a href="/wiki/Western_astrology" title="Western astrology">Western astrology</a> is a form of <a href="/wiki/Divination" title="Divination">divination</a> based on the construction of a <a href="/wiki/Horoscope" title="Horoscope">horoscope</a> for an exact moment, such as a person's birth.<sup id="cite_ref-85" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-85">[85]</a></sup> It uses the tropical zodiac, which is aligned to the <a href="/wiki/Equinox" title="Equinox">equinoctial points</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-86" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-86">[86]</a></sup></p>
<p>Western astrology is founded on the movements and relative positions of celestial bodies such as the Sun, Moon and planets, which are analysed by their movement through <a href="/wiki/Astrological_sign" title="Astrological sign">signs</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Zodiac" title="Zodiac">zodiac</a> (twelve spatial divisions of the <a href="/wiki/Ecliptic" title="Ecliptic">ecliptic</a>) and by their <a href="/wiki/Astrological_aspect" title="Astrological aspect">aspects</a> (based on geometric angles) relative to one another. They are also considered by their placement in <a href="/wiki/House_(astrology)" title="House (astrology)">houses</a> (twelve spatial divisions of the sky).<sup id="cite_ref-87" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-87">[87]</a></sup> Astrology's modern representation in western popular media is usually reduced to <a href="/wiki/Sun_sign_astrology" title="Sun sign astrology">sun sign astrology</a>, which considers only the zodiac sign of the Sun at an individual's date of birth, and represents only 1/12 of the total chart.<sup id="cite_ref-88" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-88">[88]</a></sup></p>
<p>The horoscope visually expresses the set of relationships for the time and place of the chosen event. These relationships are between the seven 'planets', signifying tendencies such as war and love; the twelve signs of the zodiac; and the twelve houses. Each planet is in a particular sign and a particular house at the chosen time, when observed from the chosen place, creating two kinds of relationship.<sup id="cite_ref-Kremer_89-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Kremer-89">[89]</a></sup> A third kind is the aspect of each planet to every other planet, where for example two planets 120Â° apart (in 'trine') are in a harmonious relationship, but two planets 90Â° apart ('square') are in a conflicted relationship.<sup id="cite_ref-90" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-90">[90]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-91" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-91">[91]</a></sup> Together these relationships and their interpretations supposedly form "...the language of the heavens speaking to learned men."<sup id="cite_ref-Kremer_89-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Kremer-89">[89]</a></sup></p>
<p>Along with <a href="/wiki/Tarot_divination" class="mw-redirect" title="Tarot divination">tarot divination</a>, astrology is one of the core studies of <a href="/wiki/Western_esotericism" title="Western esotericism">Western esotericism</a>, and as such has influenced systems of <a href="/wiki/Magic_(paranormal)" title="Magic (paranormal)">magical</a> belief not only among Western esotericists and <a href="/wiki/Hermeticism" title="Hermeticism">Hermeticists</a>, but also belief systems such as <a href="/wiki/Wicca" title="Wicca">Wicca</a> that have borrowed from or been influenced by the Western esoteric tradition. <a href="/wiki/Tanya_Luhrmann" title="Tanya Luhrmann">Tanya Luhrmann</a> has said that "all magicians know something about astrology," and refers to a <a href="/wiki/Table_of_correspondences" title="Table of correspondences">table of correspondences</a> in <a href="/wiki/Starhawk" title="Starhawk">Starhawk's</a> <i><a href="/wiki/The_Spiral_Dance" title="The Spiral Dance">The Spiral Dance</a></i>, organised by <a href="/wiki/Planets_in_astrology" title="Planets in astrology">planet</a>, as an example of the astrological lore studied by magicians.<sup id="cite_ref-Luhrmann_92-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Luhrmann-92">[92]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Hindu_2">Hindu</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Astrology&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Hindu">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Hindu_astrology" title="Hindu astrology">Hindu astrology</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Brooklyn_Museum_-_Page_from_an_Astrological_Treatise.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6e/Brooklyn_Museum_-_Page_from_an_Astrological_Treatise.jpg/170px-Brooklyn_Museum_-_Page_from_an_Astrological_Treatise.jpg" width="170" height="275" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6e/Brooklyn_Museum_-_Page_from_an_Astrological_Treatise.jpg/255px-Brooklyn_Museum_-_Page_from_an_Astrological_Treatise.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6e/Brooklyn_Museum_-_Page_from_an_Astrological_Treatise.jpg/340px-Brooklyn_Museum_-_Page_from_an_Astrological_Treatise.jpg 2x" data-file-width="475" data-file-height="768" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Brooklyn_Museum_-_Page_from_an_Astrological_Treatise.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Page from an Indian astrological treatise, c. 1750</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The earliest <a href="/wiki/Veda" class="mw-redirect" title="Veda">Vedic</a> text on astronomy is the <i><a href="/wiki/Vedanga_Jyotisha" title="Vedanga Jyotisha">Vedanga Jyotisha</a></i>; Vedic thought later came to include astrology as well.<sup id="cite_ref-Subbarayappa_93-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Subbarayappa-93">[93]</a></sup></p>
<p>Hindu natal astrology originated with Hellenistic astrology by the 3rd century BCE,<sup id="cite_ref-Pingree1978_94-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Pingree1978-94">[94]</a></sup><sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">:361</sup><sup id="cite_ref-Pingree2001_95-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Pingree2001-95">[95]</a></sup> though incorporating the Hindu lunar mansions.<sup id="cite_ref-96" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-96">[96]</a></sup> The names of the signs (e.g. Greek 'Krios' for Aries, Hindi 'Kriya'), the planets (e.g. Greek 'Helios' for Sun, astrological Hindi 'Heli'), and astrological terms (e.g. Greek 'apoklima' and 'sunaphe' for declination and planetary conjunction, Hindi 'apoklima' and 'sunapha' respectively) in Varaha Mihira's texts are considered conclusive evidence of a Greek origin for Hindu astrology.<sup id="cite_ref-97" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-97">[97]</a></sup> The Indian techniques may also have been augmented with some of the Babylonian techniques.<sup id="cite_ref-Pingree1963_98-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Pingree1963-98">[98]</a></sup><sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">:231</sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Chinese_and_East-Asian">Chinese and East-Asian</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Astrology&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Chinese and East-Asian">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote">For more details on this topic, see <a href="/wiki/Chinese_astrology" title="Chinese astrology">Chinese astrology</a> and <a href="/wiki/Chinese_zodiac" title="Chinese zodiac">Chinese zodiac</a>.</div>
<p>Chinese astrology has a close relation with <a href="/wiki/Chinese_philosophy" title="Chinese philosophy">Chinese philosophy</a> (theory of the three harmonies: heaven, earth and man) and uses concepts such as <a href="/wiki/Yin_and_yang" title="Yin and yang">yin and yang</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Wu_xing" class="mw-redirect" title="Wu xing">Five phases</a>, the 10 <a href="/wiki/Celestial_stems" class="mw-redirect" title="Celestial stems">Celestial stems</a>, the 12 <a href="/wiki/Earthly_Branches" title="Earthly Branches">Earthly Branches</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Shichen" class="mw-redirect" title="Shichen">shichen</a> (æ™‚è¾° a form of timekeeping used for religious purposes). The early use of Chinese astrology was mainly confined to <a href="/wiki/Political_astrology" class="mw-redirect" title="Political astrology">political astrology</a>, the observation of unusual phenomena, identification of <a href="/wiki/Portent_(divination)" class="mw-redirect" title="Portent (divination)">portents</a> and the selection of auspicious days for events and decisions.<sup id="cite_ref-Kistemaker_27-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Kistemaker-27">[27]</a></sup><sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">:22,85,176</sup></p>
<p>The constellations of the Zodiac of western Asia and Europe were not used; instead the sky is divided into <a href="/wiki/Three_Enclosures" class="mw-redirect" title="Three Enclosures">Three Enclosures</a> (ä¸‰åž£ sÄ?n yuÃ¡n), and <a href="/wiki/Twenty-eight_Mansions" class="mw-redirect" title="Twenty-eight Mansions">Twenty-eight Mansions</a> (äºŒå??å…«å®¿ Ã¨rshÃ­bÄ? xiÃ¹) in twelve Ci (<a href="//zh.wikipedia.org/wiki/%E5%88%86%E9%87%8E" class="extiw" title="zh:åˆ†é‡Ž">å??äºŒæ¬¡</a>).<sup id="cite_ref-99" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-99">[99]</a></sup> The Chinese zodiac of twelve <a href="/wiki/Astrological_sign#Chinese_zodiac_signs" title="Astrological sign">animal signs</a> is said to represent twelve different types of <a href="/wiki/Personality" title="Personality">personality</a>. It is based on cycles of years, lunar months, and two-hour periods of the day (the shichen). The zodiac traditionally begins with the sign of the <a href="/wiki/Rat_(zodiac)" title="Rat (zodiac)">Rat</a>, and the cycle proceeds through 11 other animals signs: the <a href="/wiki/Ox_(zodiac)" title="Ox (zodiac)">Ox</a>, <a href="/wiki/Tiger_(zodiac)" title="Tiger (zodiac)">Tiger</a>, <a href="/wiki/Rabbit_(zodiac)" title="Rabbit (zodiac)">Rabbit</a>, <a href="/wiki/Dragon_(zodiac)" title="Dragon (zodiac)">Dragon</a>, <a href="/wiki/Snake_(zodiac)" title="Snake (zodiac)">Snake</a>, <a href="/wiki/Horse_(zodiac)" title="Horse (zodiac)">Horse</a>, <a href="/wiki/Goat_(zodiac)" title="Goat (zodiac)">Goat</a>, <a href="/wiki/Monkey_(zodiac)" title="Monkey (zodiac)">Monkey</a>, <a href="/wiki/Rooster_(zodiac)" title="Rooster (zodiac)">Rooster</a>, <a href="/wiki/Dog_(zodiac)" title="Dog (zodiac)">Dog</a> and <a href="/wiki/Pig_(zodiac)" title="Pig (zodiac)">Pig</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-100" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-100">[100]</a></sup> Complex systems of predicting <a href="/wiki/Fate" class="mw-redirect" title="Fate">fate</a> and destiny based on one's birthday, birth season, and birth hours, such as <i>ziping</i> and <a href="/wiki/Zi_wei_dou_shu" title="Zi wei dou shu">Zi Wei Dou Shu</a> (<a href="/wiki/Simplified_Chinese_characters" title="Simplified Chinese characters">simplified Chinese</a>: <span lang="zh-Hans">ç´«å¾®æ–—æ•°</span>; <a href="/wiki/Traditional_Chinese_characters" title="Traditional Chinese characters">traditional Chinese</a>: <span lang="zh-Hant">ç´«å¾®æ–—æ•¸</span>; <a href="/wiki/Pinyin" title="Pinyin">pinyin</a>: <i><span lang="zh-Latn-pinyin">zÇ?wÄ“idÇ’ushÃ¹</span></i>) are still used regularly in modern-day Chinese astrology. They do not rely on direct observations of the stars.<sup id="cite_ref-101" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-101">[101]</a></sup></p>
<p>The Korean zodiac is identical to the Chinese one. The Vietnamese zodiac is almost identical to Chinese zodiac except the second animal is the <i><a href="/wiki/Water_buffalo_(zodiac)" title="Water buffalo (zodiac)">Water Buffalo</a></i> instead of the <i><a href="/wiki/Ox_(zodiac)" title="Ox (zodiac)">Ox</a></i>, and the fourth animal is the <i><a href="/wiki/Cat_(zodiac)" title="Cat (zodiac)">Cat</a></i> instead of the <i><a href="/wiki/Rabbit_(zodiac)" title="Rabbit (zodiac)">Rabbit</a></i>. The Japanese have since 1873 celebrated the beginning of the new year on 1 January as per the <a href="/wiki/Gregorian_Calendar" class="mw-redirect" title="Gregorian Calendar">Gregorian Calendar</a>. The Thai zodiac begins, not at <a href="/wiki/Chinese_New_Year" title="Chinese New Year">Chinese New Year</a>, but either on the first day of fifth month in the <a href="/wiki/Thai_lunar_calendar" title="Thai lunar calendar">Thai lunar calendar</a>, or during the <a href="/wiki/Songkran_(Thailand)" title="Songkran (Thailand)">Songkran</a> festival (now celebrated every 13â€“15 April), depending on the purpose of the use.<sup id="cite_ref-102" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-102">[102]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Theological_viewpoints">Theological viewpoints</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Astrology&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Theological viewpoints">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote">See also: <a href="/wiki/Christian_views_on_astrology" title="Christian views on astrology">Christian views on astrology</a>, <a href="/wiki/Jewish_views_on_astrology" title="Jewish views on astrology">Jewish views on astrology</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Muslim_views_on_astrology" class="mw-redirect" title="Muslim views on astrology">Muslim views on astrology</a></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Ancient">Ancient</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Astrology&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Ancient">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p><a href="/wiki/St._Augustine" class="mw-redirect" title="St. Augustine">St. Augustine</a> (354â€“430) believed that the determinism of astrology conflicted with the Christian doctrines of man's free will and responsibility, and God not being the cause of evil,<sup id="cite_ref-103" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-103">[103]</a></sup> but he also grounded his opposition philosophically, citing the failure of astrology to explain twins who behave differently although conceived at the same moment and born at approximately the same time.<sup id="cite_ref-Hess_104-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Hess-104">[104]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Medieval">Medieval</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Astrology&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Medieval">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Some of the practices of astrology were contested on theological grounds by medieval Muslim astronomers such as <a href="/wiki/Al-Farabi" title="Al-Farabi">Al-Farabi</a> (Alpharabius), <a href="/wiki/Ibn_al-Haytham" class="mw-redirect" title="Ibn al-Haytham">Ibn al-Haytham</a> (Alhazen) and <a href="/wiki/Avicenna" title="Avicenna">Avicenna</a>. They said that the methods of astrologers conflicted with orthodox religious views of <a href="/wiki/Ulema" class="mw-redirect" title="Ulema">Islamic scholars</a>, by suggesting that the Will of God can be known and predicted in advance.<sup id="cite_ref-105" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-105">[105]</a></sup> For example, Avicenna's 'Refutation against astrology', <i>RisÄ?la fÄ« ibá¹­Ä?l aá¸¥kÄ?m al-nojÅ«m</i>, argues against the practice of astrology while supporting the principle that planets may act as agents of divine causation. Avicenna considered that the movement of the planets influenced life on earth in a deterministic way, but argued against the possibility of determining the exact influence of the stars.<sup id="cite_ref-106" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-106">[106]</a></sup> Essentially, Avicenna did not deny the core dogma of astrology, but denied our ability to understand it to the extent that precise and fatalistic predictions could be made from it.<sup id="cite_ref-107" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-107">[107]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Ibn_Qayyim_Al-Jawziyya" class="mw-redirect" title="Ibn Qayyim Al-Jawziyya">Ibn Qayyim Al-Jawziyya</a> (1292â€“1350), in his <i>Miftah Dar al-SaCadah</i>, also used <a href="/wiki/Physics" title="Physics">physical</a> arguments in astronomy to question the practice of judicial astrology.<sup id="cite_ref-Livingston_108-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Livingston-108">[108]</a></sup> He recognised that the <a href="/wiki/Star" title="Star">stars</a> are much larger than the <a href="/wiki/Planet" title="Planet">planets</a>, and argued:</p>
<blockquote class="templatequote">
<p>And if you astrologers answer that it is precisely because of this distance and smallness that their influences are negligible, then why is it that you claim a great influence for the smallest heavenly body, Mercury? Why is it that you have given an influence to al-Ra's and <a href="/wiki/Al-Dhanab" class="mw-redirect" title="Al-Dhanab">al-Dhanab</a>, which are two imaginary points [ascending and descending nodes]?</p>
<div class="templatequotecite"><cite>â€”â€‰Ibn Qayyim Al-Jawziyya<sup id="cite_ref-Livingston_108-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Livingston-108">[108]</a></sup></cite></div>
</blockquote>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Modern">Modern</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Astrology&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Modern">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Catechism_of_the_Catholic_Church" title="Catechism of the Catholic Church">Catechism of the Catholic Church</a> maintains that divination, including predictive astrology, is incompatible with modern <a href="/wiki/Catholicism" title="Catholicism">Catholic</a> beliefs<sup id="cite_ref-109" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-109">[109]</a></sup> such as free will:<sup id="cite_ref-Hess_104-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Hess-104">[104]</a></sup></p>
<blockquote class="templatequote">
<p>All forms of divination are to be rejected: recourse to Satan or demons, conjuring up the dead or other practices falsely supposed to "unveil" the future. Consulting horoscopes, astrology, palm reading, interpretation of omens and lots, the phenomena of clairvoyance, and recourse to mediums all conceal a desire for power over time, history, and, in the last analysis, other human beings, as well as a wish to conciliate hidden powers. They contradict the honor, respect, and loving fear that we owe to God alone.<sup id="cite_ref-110" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-110">[110]</a></sup></p>
<div class="templatequotecite"><cite>â€”â€‰Catechism of the Catholic Church</cite></div>
</blockquote>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Scientific_analysis_and_criticism">Scientific analysis and criticism</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Astrology&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Scientific analysis and criticism">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Astrology_and_science" title="Astrology and science">Astrology and science</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Karl_Popper.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/43/Karl_Popper.jpg/170px-Karl_Popper.jpg" width="170" height="218" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/43/Karl_Popper.jpg/255px-Karl_Popper.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/43/Karl_Popper.jpg/340px-Karl_Popper.jpg 2x" data-file-width="600" data-file-height="769" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Karl_Popper.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Popper proposed falsifiability as something that distinguishes science from non-science, using astrology as the example of an idea that has not dealt with falsification during experiment</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The scientific community rejects astrology as having no explanatory power for describing the universe, and consider it a <a href="/wiki/Pseudoscience" title="Pseudoscience">pseudoscience</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-SandPSandAstroSoc_15-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-SandPSandAstroSoc-15">[15]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-astrosociety.org_16-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-astrosociety.org-16">[16]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Hartmann_17-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Hartmann-17">[17]</a></sup><sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">:1350</sup> Scientific testing of astrology has been conducted, and no evidence has been found to support any of the premises or purported effects outlined in astrological traditions.<sup id="cite_ref-Zarka_11-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Zarka-11">[11]</a></sup><sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">:424;</sup><sup id="cite_ref-111" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-111">[111]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-112" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-112">[112]</a></sup> There is no proposed mechanism of action by which the positions and motions of stars and planets could affect people and events on Earth that does not contradict well understood, basic aspects of biology and physics.<sup id="cite_ref-Vishveshwara_8-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Vishveshwara-8">[8]</a></sup><sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">:249;</sup><sup id="cite_ref-AsquithNSF_9-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-AsquithNSF-9">[9]</a></sup> Those who continue to have faith in astrology have been characterised as doing so "...in spite of the fact that there is no verified scientific basis for their beliefs, and indeed that there is strong evidence to the contrary."<sup id="cite_ref-Humanist_113-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Humanist-113">[113]</a></sup></p>
<p>It has also been shown that <a href="/wiki/Confirmation_bias" title="Confirmation bias">confirmation bias</a> is a <a href="/wiki/Psychology" title="Psychology">psychological</a> factor that contributes to belief in astrology.<sup id="cite_ref-Allum_114-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Allum-114">[114]</a></sup><sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">:344;</sup><sup id="cite_ref-Raymond_115-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Raymond-115">[115]</a></sup><sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">:180â€“181;</sup><sup id="cite_ref-Eysenck1982_116-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Eysenck1982-116">[116]</a></sup><sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">:42â€“48</sup> Confirmation bias is a form of <a href="/wiki/Cognitive_bias" title="Cognitive bias">cognitive bias</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-117" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-117">[a]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Gonzalez_118-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Gonzalez-118">[117]</a></sup><sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">:553</sup> According to available literature, astrology believers tend to selectively remember predictions that turn out to be true, and do not remember those that turn out false.
